      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_era">
        Modern era
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Toledo,_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Modern era">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Alc%C3%A1zar_of_Toledo_1823_Edward_Hawke_Locker.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="851" data-file-width="1184" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Alc%C3%A1zar_of_Toledo_1823_Edward_Hawke_Locker.jpg/220px-Alc%C3%A1zar_of_Toledo_1823_Edward_Hawke_Locker.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Alc%C3%A1zar_of_Toledo_1823_Edward_Hawke_Locker.jpg/330px-Alc%C3%A1zar_of_Toledo_1823_Edward_Hawke_Locker.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Alc%C3%A1zar_of_Toledo_1823_Edward_Hawke_Locker.jpg/440px-Alc%C3%A1zar_of_Toledo_1823_Edward_Hawke_Locker.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Alc%C3%A1zar_of_Toledo_1823_Edward_Hawke_Locker.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         View of Toledo in 1823 by
         <a href="/wiki/Edward_Hawke_Locker" title="Edward Hawke Locker">
          Edward Hawke Locker
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charles_I_of_Spain" title="Charles I of Spain">
        Charles I of Spain
       </a>
       's court was set in Toledo, serving as the imperial capital.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
        <a href="#cite_note-112">
         [112]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, in 1561, in the first years of his son
       <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Spain" title="Philip II of Spain">
        Philip II of Spain
       </a>
       's reign, the Spanish court was moved to
       <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">
        Madrid
       </a>
       , thus letting the city's importance dwindle until the late 20th century, when it became the capital of the autonomous community of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Castile%E2%80%93La_Mancha" title="Castile–La Mancha">
        Castile–La Mancha
       </a>
       . Nevertheless, the economic decline of the city helped to preserve its cultural and architectural heritage. Today, because of this rich heritage, Toledo is one of Spain's foremost cities, receiving thousands of visitors yearly.
      </p>
      <p>
       Toledo's
       <a href="/wiki/Alc%C3%A1zar_of_Toledo" title="Alcázar of Toledo">
        Alcázar
       </a>
       (Latinized Arabic word for palace-castle, from the Arabic القصر, al-qasr) became renowned in the 19th and 20th centuries as a
       <a href="/wiki/Military_academy" title="Military academy">
        military academy
       </a>
       . At the outbreak of the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">
        Spanish Civil War
       </a>
       in 1936, its garrison was famously
       <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_the_Alc%C3%A1zar" title="Siege of the Alcázar">
        besieged
       </a>
       by
       <a href="/wiki/Second_Spanish_Republic" title="Second Spanish Republic">
        Republican
       </a>
       forces.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">
        Climate
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Toledo,_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Climate">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Toledo has a typical
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cold_semi-arid_climate" title="Cold semi-arid climate">
        cold semi-arid climate
       </a>
       (Köppen:
       <i>
        BSk
       </i>
       ). Winters are cool while summers are hot and dry. Precipitation is low and mainly concentrated in the period mid autumn through to mid spring. The highest temperature ever recorded in Toledo was 43.1 °C or 109.58 °F on 10 August 2012; the lowest was −9.1 °C or 15.6 °F on 27 January 2005.
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable" style="width:90%; text-align:center; font-size:90%; line-height: 1.2em; margin:auto;">
       <caption>
        Climate data for Toledo, Spain, altitude 515 metres (1,690 feet) (1981–2010)
       </caption>
       <tr>
        <th scope="row">
         Month
        </th>
        <th scope="col">
         Jan
        </th>
        <th scope="col">
         Feb
        </th>
        <th scope="col">
         Mar
        </th>
        <th scope="col">
         Apr
        </th>
        <th scope="col">
         May
        </th>
        <th scope="col">
         Jun
        </th>
        <th scope="col">

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
        Economy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Toledo,_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Economy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Toledo_Plaza_Zocodover_1.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2872" data-file-width="4340" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Toledo_Plaza_Zocodover_1.jpg/220px-Toledo_Plaza_Zocodover_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Toledo_Plaza_Zocodover_1.jpg/330px-Toledo_Plaza_Zocodover_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Toledo_Plaza_Zocodover_1.jpg/440px-Toledo_Plaza_Zocodover_1.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Toledo_Plaza_Zocodover_1.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <i>
          Zocodover square
         </i>
         after the Corpus Christi festivities.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The metal-working industry has historically been Toledo's economic base, with a great tradition in the manufacturing of swords and knives and a significant production of razor blades, medical devices and electrical products. (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Toledo_Blade" title="The Toledo Blade">
        The Toledo Blade
       </a>
       , the American newspaper in Toledo's
       <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">
        Ohio
       </a>
       namesake city, is named in honor of the sword-making tradition.) Soap and toothpaste industries, flour milling, glass and ceramics have also been important.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-economia_114-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-economia-114">
         [114]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Goya_Foods" title="Goya Foods">
        Goya Foods
       </a>
       has its Madrid offices in Toledo.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">
        <a href="#cite_note-115">
         [115]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Toledo_Museo_Santa_Cruz_1.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4212" data-file-width="2772" height="258" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Toledo_Museo_Santa_Cruz_1.jpg/170px-Toledo_Museo_Santa_Cruz_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Toledo_Museo_Santa_Cruz_1.jpg/255px-Toledo_Museo_Santa_Cruz_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Toledo_Museo_Santa_Cruz_1.jpg/340px-Toledo_Museo_Santa_Cruz_1.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Toledo_Museo_Santa_Cruz_1.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The Museum
         <i>
          Santa Cruz
         </i>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1_Puerta_de_Bisagra_toledo_2014.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4912" data-file-width="7360" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/1_Puerta_de_Bisagra_toledo_2014.jpg/220px-1_Puerta_de_Bisagra_toledo_2014.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/1_Puerta_de_Bisagra_toledo_2014.jpg/330px-1_Puerta_de_Bisagra_toledo_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/1_Puerta_de_Bisagra_toledo_2014.jpg/440px-1_Puerta_de_Bisagra_toledo_2014.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1_Puerta_de_Bisagra_toledo_2014.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <i>
          Puerta de Bisagra
         </i>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The manufacture of swords in the city of Toledo goes back to
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">
        Roman
       </a>
       times, but it was under
       <a href="/wiki/Al-Andalus" title="Al-Andalus">
        Moorish
       </a>
       rule and during the
       <a href="/wiki/Reconquista" title="Reconquista">
        Reconquista
       </a>
       that Toledo and its guild of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swordsmith" title="Swordsmith">
        sword-makers
       </a>
       played a key role. Between the 15th and 17th centuries the Toledo sword-making industry enjoyed a great boom, to the point where its
       <a href="/wiki/Toledo_steel" title="Toledo steel">
        products
       </a>
       came to be regarded as the best in Europe. Swords and daggers were made by individual craftsmen, although the sword-makers guild oversaw their quality. In the late 17th and early 18th century production began to decline, prompting the creation of the Royal Arms Factory in 1761 by order of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_Carlos_III" title="King Carlos III">
        King Carlos III
       </a>
       . The Royal Factory brought together all the sword-makers guilds of the city and it was located in the former mint. In 1777, recognizing the need to expand the space, Carlos III commissioned the architect
       <a href="/wiki/Francesco_Sabatini" title="Francesco Sabatini">
        Sabatini
       </a>
       to construct a new building on the outskirts of the city. This was the beginning of several phases of expansion. Its importance was such that it eventually developed into a city within the city of Toledo.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Souvenirs_from_Toledo.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Souvenirs_from_Toledo.jpg/220px-Souvenirs_from_Toledo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Souvenirs_from_Toledo.jpg/330px-Souvenirs_from_Toledo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Souvenirs_from_Toledo.jpg/440px-Souvenirs_from_Toledo.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Souvenirs_from_Toledo.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Historical swords and souvenirs of Toledo.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In the 20th century, the production of knives and swords for the army was reduced to cavalry weapons only, and after the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">
        Spanish Civil War
       </a>
       , to the supply of swords to the officers and NCOs of the various military units. Following the closure of the factory in the 1980s, the building was renovated to house the campus of the Technological University of Castilla-La Mancha in Toledo.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ref_duplicada_1_116-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ref_duplicada_1-116">
         [116]
        </a>
       </sup>
       According to the Statistical Institute of Castilla-La Mancha, in 2007 the recent distribution of employment by sectors of occupation was as follows: 86.5% of the population engaged in the services, 6.6% in construction, 5.4% in industry and 1.5% in agriculture and livestock.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-estadistica_117-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-estadistica-117">
         [117]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Unemployment">
        Unemployment
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Toledo,_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Unemployment">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In the last decade, unemployment in absolute terms has remained fairly stable in the city of Toledo, but in 2009 this figure increased significantly: nearly 62% compared to 2008, with the number of unemployed rising from 2,515 to 4,074 (figures at 31 March each year), according to the Junta de Comunidades de Castilla La Mancha.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-paro_118-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-paro-118">
         [118]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Of this 62%, one third of the increase took place in the first quarter.
      </p>
      <p>
       According to other statistics from the same source, almost half the unemployed in the city of Toledo (1,970 persons) are among those whose education does not go beyond the compulsory secondary level. However, there are groups whose level of studies is such that they have not been registered as unemployed, such as those who have completed class 1 professional training, or those with virtually nonexistent unemployment rates (less than 0.1%), which is the case of unemployed with high school degrees or professional expertise.
      </p>
      <p>
       The largest group among the unemployed is those who have no qualifications (27.27%).
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">
        Politics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Toledo,_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Politics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Toledo_(Spain)" title="Politics of Toledo (Spain)">
        Politics of Toledo (Spain)
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Toledo,_Ayuntamiento-PM_65578.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="808" data-file-width="1000" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Toledo%2C_Ayuntamiento-PM_65578.jpg/220px-Toledo%2C_Ayuntamiento-PM_65578.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Toledo%2C_Ayuntamiento-PM_65578.jpg/330px-Toledo%2C_Ayuntamiento-PM_65578.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Toledo%2C_Ayuntamiento-PM_65578.jpg/440px-Toledo%2C_Ayuntamiento-PM_65578.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Toledo,_Ayuntamiento-PM_65578.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Toledo City Hall.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Toledo has a 25-member City Council, elected by closed lists every four years. The 2011 election saw a pact made between the 11 members of the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Socialist_Workers%27_Party" title="Spanish Socialist Workers' Party">
        Spanish Socialist Workers' Party
       </a>
       (PSOE) and the 2 members of the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Left_(Spain)" title="United Left (Spain)">
        United Left
       </a>
       , to retain the position of the PSOE's Emiliano García-Page Sánchez as mayor, which he has been since 2007.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">
        Culture
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Toledo,_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Culture">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The old city is located on a mountaintop with a 150 degree view, surrounded on three sides by a bend in the
       <a href="/wiki/Tagus" title="Tagus">
        Tagus River
       </a>
       , and contains many historical sites, including the
       <a href="/wiki/Alc%C3%A1zar_of_Toledo" title="Alcázar of Toledo">
        Alcázar
       </a>
       , the cathedral (the
       <a href="/wiki/Primate_(bishop)" title="Primate (bishop)">
        primate
       </a>
       church of Spain), and the Zocodover, a central market place.
      </p>
      <p>
       From the 4th century to the 16th century about thirty
       <a href="/wiki/Synod" title="Synod">
        synods
       </a>
       were held at Toledo. The earliest, directed against
       <a href="/wiki/Priscillian" title="Priscillian">
        Priscillian
       </a>
       , assembled in 400. At the synod of 589 the Visigothic King
       <a href="/wiki/Reccared_I" title="Reccared I">
        Reccared
       </a>
       declared his conversion from
       <a href="/wiki/Arianism" title="Arianism">
        Arianism
       </a>
       to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholicism" title="Catholicism">
        Catholicism
       </a>
       ; the synod of 633 decreed uniformity of catholic liturgy throughout the Visigothic kingdom and took stringent measures against baptized Jews who had relapsed into their former faith. Other councils forbade circumcision, Jewish rites and observance of the Sabbath and festivals. Throughout the seventh century, Jews were flogged, executed, had their property confiscated, were subjected to ruinous taxes, forbidden to trade and, at times, dragged to the baptismal font.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">
        <a href="#cite_note-119">
         [119]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The council of 681 assured to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archdiocese_of_Toledo" title="Archdiocese of Toledo">
        archbishop of Toledo
       </a>
       the
       <a href="/wiki/Primate_(bishop)" title="Primate (bishop)">
        primacy
       </a>
       of Spain. At
       <a href="/wiki/Guadamur" title="Guadamur">
        Guadamur
       </a>
       , very close to Toledo, was dug in 1858 the
       <a href="/wiki/Treasure_of_Guarrazar" title="Treasure of Guarrazar">
        Treasure of Guarrazar
       </a>
       , the best example of
       <a href="/wiki/Visigothic_art_and_architecture" title="Visigothic art and architecture">
        Visigothic art
       </a>
       in Spain.
      </p>
      <p>
       As nearly one hundred early canons of Toledo found a place in the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Decretum_Gratiani" title="Decretum Gratiani">
         Decretum Gratiani
        </a>
       </i>
       , they exerted an important influence on the development of
       <a href="/wiki/Canon_law" title="Canon law">
        ecclesiastical law
       </a>
       . The synod of 1565–1566 concerned itself with the execution of the decrees of the
       <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Trent" title="Council of Trent">
        Council of Trent
       </a>
       ; and the last council held at Toledo, 1582–1583, was guided in detail by
       <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Spain" title="Philip II of Spain">
        Philip II
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Toledo had large communities of Muslims and Jews until they were
       <a href="/wiki/Alhambra_Decree" title="Alhambra Decree">
        expelled from Spain in 1492
       </a>
       (Jews) and 1502 (
       <a href="/wiki/Mud%C3%A9jar" title="Mudéjar">
        Mudéjars
       </a>
       ). Today's city contains the religious monuments the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_la_Blanca" title="Santa María la Blanca">
        Synagogue of Santa María la Blanca
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Synagogue_of_El_Transito" title="Synagogue of El Transito">
        Synagogue of El Transito
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mosque_of_Cristo_de_la_Luz" title="Mosque of Cristo de la Luz">
        Mosque of Cristo de la Luz
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Church_of_San_Sebasti%C3%A1n,_Toledo" title="Church of San Sebastián, Toledo">
        church of San Sebastián
       </a>
       dating from before the expulsion, still maintained in good condition. Among
       <a href="/wiki/Judaeo-Spanish" title="Judaeo-Spanish">
        Ladino
       </a>
       -speaking
       <a href="/wiki/Sephardi_Jews" title="Sephardi Jews">
        Sephardi Jews
       </a>
       , in their various diasporas, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Family_name" title="Family name">
        family name
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Toledano" title="Toledano">
        Toledano
       </a>
       is still prevalent—indicating an ancestry traced back to this city (the name is also attested among non-Jews in various
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish-speaking countries
       </a>
       ).
      </p>
      <p>
       In the 13th century, Toledo was a major cultural centre under the guidance of
       <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_X_of_Castile" title="Alfonso X of Castile">
        Alfonso X
       </a>
       , called "El Sabio" ("the Wise") for his love of learning. The
       <a href="/wiki/Toledo_School_of_Translators" title="Toledo School of Translators">
        Toledo School of Translators
       </a>
       , that had commenced under Archbishop
       <a href="/wiki/Raymond_de_Sauvet%C3%A2t" title="Raymond de Sauvetât">
        Raymond of Toledo
       </a>
       , continued to bring vast stores of knowledge to Europe by rendering great academic and philosophical works in Arabic into Latin. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palacio_de_Galiana" title="Palacio de Galiana">
        Palacio de Galiana
       </a>
       , built in the
       <a href="/wiki/Mud%C3%A9jar" title="Mudéjar">
        Mudéjar
       </a>
       style, is one of the monuments that remain from that period.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Toledo" title="Cathedral of Toledo">
        Cathedral of Toledo
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        Catedral de Toledo
       </i>
       ) was built between 1226–1493 and modeled after the
       <a href="/wiki/Bourges_Cathedral" title="Bourges Cathedral">
        Bourges Cathedral
       </a>
       , though it also combines some characteristics of the
       <a href="/wiki/Mud%C3%A9jar" title="Mudéjar">
        Mudéjar
       </a>
       style. It is remarkable for its incorporation of light and features the
       <a href="/wiki/Baroque" title="Baroque">
        Baroque
       </a>
       altar called
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/El_Transparente" title="El Transparente">
         El Transparente
        </a>
       </i>
       , several stories high, with fantastic figures of stucco, paintings, bronze castings, and multiple colors of marble, a masterpiece of
       <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">
        medieval
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Mixed_media" title="Mixed media">
        mixed media
       </a>
       by
       <a href="/wiki/Narciso_Tom%C3%A9" title="Narciso Tomé">
        Narciso Tomé
       </a>
       topped by the daily effect for just a few minutes of a shaft of light from which this feature of the cathedral derives its name. Two notable bridges secured access to Toledo across the Tajo, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puente_de_Alc%C3%A1ntara,_Toledo" title="Puente de Alcántara, Toledo">
        Alcántara bridge
       </a>
       and the later built
       <a href="/wiki/Puente_de_San_Mart%C3%ADn_(Toledo)" title="Puente de San Martín (Toledo)">
        San Martín bridge
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monasterio_de_San_Juan_de_los_Reyes,_Toledo" title="Monasterio de San Juan de los Reyes, Toledo">
        Monasterio de San Juan de los Reyes
       </a>
       is a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Franciscan" title="Franciscan">
        Franciscan
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Monastery" title="Monastery">
        monastery
       </a>
       , built 1477–1504, in a remarkable combination of Gothic-Spanish-Flemish style with
       <a href="/wiki/Mud%C3%A9jar" title="Mudéjar">
        Mudéjar
       </a>
       ornamentation.
      </p>
      <p>
       Toledo was home to
       <a href="/wiki/El_Greco" title="El Greco">
        El Greco
       </a>
       for the latter part of his life, and is the subject of some of his most famous paintings, including
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Burial_of_the_Count_of_Orgaz" title="The Burial of the Count of Orgaz">
         The Burial of the Count of Orgaz
        </a>
       </i>
       , exhibited in the Church of Santo Tomé.
      </p>
      <p>
       When Philip II moved the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_court" title="Royal court">
        royal court
       </a>
       from Toledo to
       <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">
        Madrid
       </a>
       in 1561, the old city went into a slow decline from which it never recovered.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Toledo_steel">
        Toledo steel
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Toledo,_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Toledo steel">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Toledo has been a traditional sword-making, steel-working centre since about 500 BC, and came to the attention of Rome when used by
       <a href="/wiki/Hannibal" title="Hannibal">
        Hannibal
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Punic_Wars" title="Punic Wars">
        Punic Wars
       </a>
       . Soon, it became a standard source of weaponry for
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_legion" title="Roman legion">
        Roman Legions
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">
        <a href="#cite_note-120">
         [120]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Toledo_steel" title="Toledo steel">
        Toledo steel
       </a>
       was famed for its very high quality
       <a href="/wiki/Alloy" title="Alloy">
        alloy
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">
        <a href="#cite_note-121">
         [121]
        </a>
       </sup>
       whereas
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Damascene_steel" title="Damascene steel">
        Damascene steel
       </a>
       , a competitor from the
       <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">
        Middle Ages
       </a>
       on, was famed for a specific metal-working technique.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">
        <a href="#cite_note-122">
         [122]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Today there is a significant trade, and many shops offer all kinds of swords to their customers, whether
       <a class="external text" href="http://www.elartedetoledo.com/espadas-historicas-9-c.asp" rel="nofollow">
        historical or modern films swords, as well as medieval armors and from other times
       </a>
       , which are also exported to other countries.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Gastronomy">
        Gastronomy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Toledo,_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Gastronomy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1_Iglesia_de_San_Ildelfonso_toledo_2014.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="7360" data-file-width="4912" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/1_Iglesia_de_San_Ildelfonso_toledo_2014.jpg/170px-1_Iglesia_de_San_Ildelfonso_toledo_2014.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/1_Iglesia_de_San_Ildelfonso_toledo_2014.jpg/255px-1_Iglesia_de_San_Ildelfonso_toledo_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/1_Iglesia_de_San_Ildelfonso_toledo_2014.jpg/340px-1_Iglesia_de_San_Ildelfonso_toledo_2014.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1_Iglesia_de_San_Ildelfonso_toledo_2014.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Inside Iglesia de San Ildelfonso, a Jesuit church.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Toledo's cuisine is grouped with that of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Castilian-Manchego_cuisine" title="Castilian-Manchego cuisine">
        Castile–La Mancha
       </a>
       , well-set in its traditions and closely linked to hunting and grazing. A good number of recipes are the result of a combination of Moorish and Christian influences.
      </p>
      <p>
       Some of its specialties include lamb roast or stew,
       <i>
        cochifrito
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        alubias con perdiz
       </i>
       (beans with partridge) and
       <i>
        perdiz estofoda
       </i>
       (partridge stew),
       <i>
        carcamusa
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Migas" title="Migas">
         migas
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Gachas#Castile-La_Mancha" title="Gachas">
         gachas manchegas
        </a>
       </i>
       , and
       <i>
        tortilla a la magra
       </i>
       . Two of the city's most famous food productions are Manchego cheese and
       <a href="/wiki/Marzipan" title="Marzipan">
        marzipan
       </a>
       , which has a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protected_Geographical_Indication" title="Protected Geographical Indication">
        Protected Geographical Indication
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        mazapán de Toledo
       </i>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gastronomia_123-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-gastronomia-123">
         [123]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-platos_típicos_124-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-platos_típicos-124">
         [124]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Holidays">
        Holidays
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Toledo,_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Holidays">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Virgen del Valle: This pilgrimage is celebrated on May 1 at the Ermita de la Virgen del Valle, with a concentration popular holiday in that place.
       </li>
       <li>
        Holy Week: Declared of National Tourist Interest, is held in spring with various processions, highlighting those that take place on Good Friday, and religious and cultural events. Since the Civil War, most of the steps were burned or destroyed, so it had to create new steps or using images from other churches and convents Toledo. Being a city Toledo Castile, Holy Week is characterized as austere and introspective, as well as beauty, due in part to the beautiful framework in which it takes place: Toledo. Many people take advantage of the Easter break to visit the monastery churches that are only open to the general public at this time of year. [42]
       </li>
       <li>
        Corpus Christi: Feast declared International Tourist Interest. Its origins lie in the thirteenth century and is probably the most beautiful Corpus Christi there. The processional cortege travels around two kilometres (1.2 miles) of streets and richly decorated awnings. In recent years, following the transfer of the traditional holiday Thursday present Sunday, was chosen to conduct two processions, one each of these days, with certain differences in members and protocol between them. [43]
       </li>
       <li>
        Virgen del Sagrario: On August 15 they celebrate the festival in honor of the Virgen del Sagrario. Procession is held inside the Cathedral and drinking water of the Virgin in jars.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Apart from these festivals should be noted that patterns of Toledo are:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ildephonsus_of_Toledo" title="Ildephonsus of Toledo">
         San Ildefonso
        </a>
        , Toledo Visigoth bishop whose feast day is January 23.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Leocadia" title="Leocadia">
         Santa Leocadia
        </a>
        , virgin and martyr of Roman Hispania, which falls on December 9.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Main_sights">
        Main sights
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Toledo,_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Main sights">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:001_Alcantara_-_the_roman_bridge.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2874" data-file-width="3856" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/001_Alcantara_-_the_roman_bridge.jpg/220px-001_Alcantara_-_the_roman_bridge.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/001_Alcantara_-_the_roman_bridge.jpg/330px-001_Alcantara_-_the_roman_bridge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/001_Alcantara_-_the_roman_bridge.jpg/440px-001_Alcantara_-_the_roman_bridge.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:001_Alcantara_-_the_roman_bridge.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Alcantara Bridge, Collotype 1889.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The city of Toledo was declared a Historic-Artistic Site in 1940, UNESCO later given the title of World Heritage in 1987. Sights include:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Tomb of
        <a href="/wiki/Beatrice_of_Silva" title="Beatrice of Silva">
         Saint Beatrice of Silva
        </a>
        , founder of the Order of the Immaculate Conception, at the
        <a href="/wiki/Conceptionists" title="Conceptionists">
         Conceptionist Monastery
        </a>
        of Toledo.
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Castillo_de_San_Servando" title="Castillo de San Servando">
          Castillo de San Servando
         </a>
        </i>
        , medieval castle near the banks of the Tagus river and the Infantry Academy.
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">
         Gothic
        </a>
        <a href="/wiki/Toledo_Cathedral" title="Toledo Cathedral">
         Cathedral
        </a>
        , dating from the thirteenth century. Inside there is the Clear from Narciso Tome, in Baroque.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monasterio_de_San_Juan_de_los_Reyes,_Toledo" title="Monasterio de San Juan de los Reyes, Toledo">
         Monasterio de San Juan de los Reyes
        </a>
        , in
        <a href="/wiki/Isabelline_Gothic" title="Isabelline Gothic">
         Isabelline Gothic
        </a>
        style (15th century).
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Santa_Cruz" title="Museum of Santa Cruz">
         Renaissance Museo-Hospital de Santa Cruz
        </a>
        (16th century).
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/El_Greco_Museum,_Toledo" title="El Greco Museum, Toledo">
         El Greco Museum
        </a>
        , a house-museum designed as a recreation of the artist's home, which was lost centuries ago. It houses several important paintings.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_la_Blanca" title="Santa María la Blanca">
         Santa María la Blanca
        </a>
        , the oldest synagogue building in Europe still standing, now owned by the Catholic Church.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Synagogue_of_El_Transito" title="Synagogue of El Transito">
         Synagogue of El Transito
        </a>
        , in the Jewish Quarter. It is home to the Sephardic Museum.
       </li>
       <li>
        Hospital de Tavera Museum Duque de Lerma. Renaissance style, dates from the sixteenth century. Influenced the layout of El Escorial.
       </li>
       <li>
        Church of
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santiago_del_Arrabal" title="Santiago del Arrabal">
         Santiago del Arrabal
        </a>
        , in Mudéjar style.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Iglesia_de_Santo_Tom%C3%A9,_Toledo" title="Iglesia de Santo Tomé, Toledo">
         Iglesia de Santo Tome
        </a>
        . Mudéjar style, the fourteenth century, houses the famous Burial of Count Orgaz, by El Greco.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/El_Cristo_de_la_Luz" title="El Cristo de la Luz">
         El Cristo de la Luz
        </a>
        , a small mosque-oratory built in 999, later extended with Mudéjar apse for conversion into a church.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galiana_Palace" title="Galiana Palace">
         Galiana Palace
        </a>
        (13th century), in Mudéjar style.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Torner%C3%ADas_Mosque" title="Tornerías Mosque">
         Tornerías Mosque
        </a>
        (11th century).
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alcazar_of_Toledo" title="Alcazar of Toledo">
         Alcazar
        </a>
        fortress (16th century), located in the highest part of town, overlooking the city. From 2009 it houses the collection of the Army Museum.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Puerta_Bab_al-Mardum" title="Puerta Bab al-Mardum">
         Puerta Bab al-Mardum
        </a>
        (10th century), the oldest city gate of Toledo.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Puerta_de_Bisagra" title="Puerta de Bisagra">
         Puerta de Bisagra Antigua
        </a>
        (10th century), the main entrance to the city in Andalusian times. Also known as "Puerta de Alfonso VI".
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Puerta_del_Sol,_Toledo" title="Puerta del Sol, Toledo">
         Puerta del Sol
        </a>
        (14th century), built by the Knights Hospitallers in Mudéjar style.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Puerta_de_Bisagra_Nueva" title="Puerta de Bisagra Nueva">
         Puerta de Bisagra Nueva
        </a>
        (16th century), of Moorish origin re-built by Alonso de Covarrubias. The main entrance and face of Toledo today.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Puerta_del_Cambr%C3%B3n" title="Puerta del Cambrón">
         Puerta del Cambrón
        </a>
        , of Muslim origin, re-built in the 16th century.
       </li>
       <li>
        San Román (Museum of the Councils and Visigoth culture).
       </li>
       <li>
        Ermita del Cristo de la Vega, in Mudéjar style (11th century).
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puente_de_Alc%C3%A1ntara,_Toledo" title="Puente de Alcántara, Toledo">
         Alcántara bridge
        </a>
        , Roman bridge across the Tagus.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Puente_de_San_Mart%C3%ADn_(Toledo)" title="Puente de San Martín (Toledo)">
         Puente de San Martin
        </a>
        , medieval bridge across the Tagus.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       To mark the fourth centenary of the publication of the first part of
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Don_Quixote" title="Don Quixote">
         Don Quixote
        </a>
       </i>
       , the Council of Communities of Castile–La Mancha designed a series of routes through the region crossing the various points cited in the novel. Known as the Route of Don Quixote, two of the pathways designated, sections 1 and 8, are based in Toledo; those linking the city with La Mancha Castile and Montes de Toledo exploit the natural route which passes through the Cigarrales and heads to Cobisa, Nambroca Burguillos of Toledo, where it takes the Camino Real from Sevilla to suddenly turn towards Mascaraque Almonacid de Toledo, deep into their surroundings, near Mora, in La Mancha.
      </p>
      <p>
       This stretch, Mascaraque-Toledo, of the Route of Don Quixote has recently been included in an official way on the Camino de Santiago in Levantine branch with origins in Cartagena, Alicante and Valencia, as both routes are declared a European Cultural Route on this stretch.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">
        Infrastructure
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Toledo,_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Puerta_de_Cambr%C3%B3n,_Toledo.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3144" data-file-width="2525" height="212" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Puerta_de_Cambr%C3%B3n%2C_Toledo.jpg/170px-Puerta_de_Cambr%C3%B3n%2C_Toledo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Puerta_de_Cambr%C3%B3n%2C_Toledo.jpg/255px-Puerta_de_Cambr%C3%B3n%2C_Toledo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Puerta_de_Cambr%C3%B3n%2C_Toledo.jpg/340px-Puerta_de_Cambr%C3%B3n%2C_Toledo.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Puerta_de_Cambr%C3%B3n,_Toledo.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Cambrón Gate.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Toledo has long been an obligatory stop in the centre of the peninsula. The roads leading to historic Toledo are still used and in many cases have provided the basis to existing roads leading into the city.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Roads">
        Roads
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Toledo,_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Roads">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       From Toledo part of N-400, which links this city with Cuenca by Ocaña and Tarancón. It is currently in the process of transformation in the future A-40 motorway Castilla La Mancha, which will link Maqueda (where it joins the motorway Extremadura), Toledo, Ocaña (where it attaches to the Motorway of Andalusia), Tarancón (where connects with the motorway Levante), Cuenca and Teruel.
      </p>
      <p>
       The old National Road 401 Madrid-Toledo-Ciudad Real was transformed in the late 1980s in the current A-42 as a result of splitting and deleting the path that the various crossings counted (Illescas, Yuncos, etc.. ).
      </p>
      <p>
       The split path can take 7 kilometres (4 miles) south of Toledo, in effect Ciudad Real, where it continues as conventional road. At this point, the A-42 connects with the Highway of the Vineyard that reaches Tomelloso. It is planned to extend the A-42, by a toll road, to Ciudad Real and Jaén.
      </p>
      <p>
       In the early twenty-first century was built, in order to decongest the access of Madrid, the toll motorway AP-41.
      </p>
      <p>
       Another way of State Highway Network that Toledo is part of the N-403, Toledo-Maqueda – Ávila – Adanero. Part of the route of this road will be replaced by that of the aforementioned Highway of Castilla La Mancha.
      </p>
      <p>
       In addition to these roads, from Toledo depart several regional and provincial-level linking the capital with the regions of Montes de Toledo, La Jara and La Mancha.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">
        Rail
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Toledo,_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Rail">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Train_station_of_Toledo,_Spain_01.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2729" data-file-width="1868" height="248" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Train_station_of_Toledo%2C_Spain_01.jpg/170px-Train_station_of_Toledo%2C_Spain_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Train_station_of_Toledo%2C_Spain_01.jpg/255px-Train_station_of_Toledo%2C_Spain_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Train_station_of_Toledo%2C_Spain_01.jpg/340px-Train_station_of_Toledo%2C_Spain_01.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Train_station_of_Toledo,_Spain_01.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toledo_Railway_Station" title="Toledo Railway Station">
          Toledo Railway Station
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In the mid-nineteenth century Toledo was one of the first Spanish cities to receive rail service, being attached to the Madrid – Aranjuez line which was inaugurated by Isabella II on June 12 of 1858. The current station is in
       <a href="/wiki/Neo-Mud%C3%A9jar" title="Neo-Mudéjar">
        Neo-Mudéjar
       </a>
       style, and was inaugurated on April 24 of 1919. It is a remarkably beautiful building, especially the paneling in the main hall of the same.
      </p>
      <p>
       With several ups and downs in terms of technical equipment and services this is the line that served the city until the early twenty-first century: on July 2 of 2003 the last conventional train service between the two capitals ended and work began on the high-speed link, Madrid – Toledo, which entered service on November 16 of 2005, thanks to which travel time to Madrid has been reduced to just under 30 minutes.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Health">
        Health
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Toledo,_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Health">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1_hospital_tavera_2014.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4912" data-file-width="7360" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/1_hospital_tavera_2014.jpg/220px-1_hospital_tavera_2014.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/1_hospital_tavera_2014.jpg/330px-1_hospital_tavera_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/1_hospital_tavera_2014.jpg/440px-1_hospital_tavera_2014.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1_hospital_tavera_2014.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Hospital of Tavera (built between 1541–1603).
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In the early 1960s began the construction of the Residence Health Social Security "Virgen de la Salud". The original building still remains in use, although successive extensions were added (maternity, outpatient clinics, operating rooms, etc.) into the existing complex. The complex was also extended to move the clinic to a new nearby building, now converted into Specialty Centre
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ildephonsus_of_Toledo" title="Ildephonsus of Toledo">
        San Ildefonso
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       On October 6, 1974 inaugurated the National Hospital of Paraplegics who becomes the centre of reference, both nationally and internationally, in the treatment of these lesions. Also carries out a major work of social integration of their patients.
      </p>
      <p>
       The transfer of powers from the state health at the Junta de Comunidades de Castilla La Mancha will give new impetus to the health infrastructure, manifested in 2007 with the commencement of construction of the new General Hospital of Toledo in the Santa Mary Benquerencia. Also have been provided to the different parts of the relevant health centres.
      </p>
      <p>
       In the Toledo Hospital Complex [36] is also integrated Geriatric Hospital Virgen del Valle, a result of reform and modernization of old tuberculosis hospital built in the mid twentieth century. The centre is located outside the city, near the Parador Nacional de Turismo Conde de Orgaz.
      </p>
      <p>
       With regard to private health, at present the city of Toledo has several centres: Hospital de las Tres Culturas, Clínica Nuestra Señora del Rosario, and so on.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">
        Sport
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Toledo,_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Sport">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Toledo suffered from a shortage of sports facilities.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Much of this problem was resolved when the Central School of Physical Education of the Army moved its headquarters to the premises of the Academy of Infantry. In the 1990s, the city council took over the old facilities of the military centre, which now include an athletics track, Olympic swimming pool and an indoor sports hall, from the former military installations, and numerous outdoor courts built in the area of the former runway of application, having been demolished and the old gym complex pools (indoor and outdoor).
      </p>
      <p>
       Besides these facilities, the city of Toledo has covered sports pavilions in the districts of Santa Maria de Benquerencia, Santa Barbara, San Anton (Complejo Deportivo "Leaping Horse"), outdoor pools in sugar, Palomarejos, Santa Maria de Benquerencia, Santa Barbara, Santa Teresa and indoor swimming pools in the gardens of the Alcazar (old town), Santa Maria de Benquerencia and San Antonio.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Toledo has a football team,
       <a href="/wiki/CD_Toledo" title="CD Toledo">
        Club Deportivo Toledo
       </a>
       , which is currently
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">
          <span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (August 2015)">
           when?
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       playing in the third-tier
       <a href="/wiki/Segunda_Divisi%C3%B3n_B" title="Segunda División B">
        Segunda División B
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       The club plays its matches in the municipal field Leaping Horse, opened in 1973. The team played for 7 seasons in the
       <a href="/wiki/Segunda_Divisi%C3%B3n" title="Segunda División">
        Segunda División
       </a>
       , during which it reached the play-off final for promotion to
       <a href="/wiki/La_Liga" title="La Liga">
        La Liga
       </a>
       at the end of the 1993–94 season, losing 4–1 on aggregate to
       <a href="/wiki/Real_Valladolid" title="Real Valladolid">
        Real Valladolid
       </a>
       . Toledo players have included
       <a href="/wiki/Abel_Resino" title="Abel Resino">
        Abel Resino
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Luis_Garc%C3%ADa_Sanz" title="Luis García Sanz">
        Luis Garcia
       </a>
       , Rufete and Casquero.
      </p>
      <p>
       Toledo also has teams of handball.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       The Toledo Handball, after five years in the Division de Honor B, start the 2009–2010 season as ASOBAL new club for the first time in its history. A refurbished town hall "Javier Lozano Cid ', with capacity for around 1,500 spectators, is its new headquarters. Moreover, the city has two other Division II team in the National, the Toledo Handball Lábaro-B and Club Deportivo Amibal.
      </p>
      <p>
       Toledo has two basketball teams: the CIS Toledo, with a long history that has gone through ups and downs in both regional and in national leagues (EBA) and has just
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">
          <span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (August 2015)">
           when?
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       promoted to 1st Autonomic, and CB Polígono, currently the most representative, whose team has promoted male, seven years after leaving, to EBA League to start the 2009/10 season.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       This club based in the Santa Maria de Benquerencia district and has one of the largest quarries of Castilla-La Mancha.
      </p>
      <p>
       Toledo has been represented in athletics since 2 April 1979 by the Toledo Athletic Club, that is characterised by its actions, mainly in cross-country, where he managed a large number of medals in the championships team Spain's specialty, in addition to their combined male and female military in the late 1990s in the 1st division league national track. Among the athletes who have passed through its lanes are great athletes as Julio Rey, Roberto Parra, Chema Martinez and Julia Lobato.
      </p>
      <p>
       Cycling, meanwhile, after the victory in the
       <a href="/wiki/Tour_de_France" title="Tour de France">
        Tour de France
       </a>
       in 1959 by
       <a href="/wiki/Federico_Bahamontes" title="Federico Bahamontes">
        Federico Bahamontes
       </a>
       , 'The Eagle of Toledo', has been one of the sports with more followers in the city, although, at present,
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">
          <span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (August 2015)">
           when?
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       no school despite having a velodrome in Santa María de Benquerencia.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Other leading professional cyclists from the city have been Nemesio Jiménez (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mexico_Olympics_1968" title="Mexico Olympics 1968">
        Mexico Olympics 1968
       </a>
       ) and Ángel de las Heras.
      </p>
      <p>
       The FS and Volleyball Toledo Toledo Association Toledo complete representation in the National League of First and Second Division, after a brief journey in Fantasy, respectively, while the Toledo Rugby Club, with manyfans, is immersed in the League Madrid's Primera Liga.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       At the individual level, the swimmer Javier Noriega and Julio Rey marathon athletes are more representative of the city, both in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Athens_Olympics_2004" title="Athens Olympics 2004">
        Athens Olympics 2004
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beijing_Olympics_2008" title="Beijing Olympics 2008">
        Beijing Olympics 2008
       </a>
       , in recent years. Rey, Spanish current marathon record holder, with 2h.06:52, announced his retirement in October 2009.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Media">
        Media
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Toledo,_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Media">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Various local and provincial newspapers are published in the city. In addition, national newspapers such as the daily ABC publish unique local editions.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Among the local newspapers are the subscription-based La Tribuna de Toledo, and Toledo Day, as well as the free Global Castilla la Mancha and Toledo News. The general information weekly magazines Echoes and Here are also published.
      </p>
      <p>
       There is also local media in television, radio and Internet. The regional public television headquarters, CMT, are in Toledo.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       In addition, there are several local television stations, as well as local fare: the diocesan Popular TV, Teletoledo, Canal Regional de Noticia and La Tribuna TV.
      </p>
      <p>
       For radio stations, there is the dean of radio Radio Toledo (Onda Cero), as well as COPE, Cadena SER, RNE, RCM and Radio Aquí, and the local fare Onda Polígono and the diocesan station Radio Santa Maria. Within the digital and social media, Onda Toledo, Toledo Magic, Toledo Digital, and La Cerca.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">
        In popular culture
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Toledo,_Spain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: In popular culture">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Segundo_de_Chom%C3%B3n" title="Segundo de Chomón">
        Segundo de Chomón
       </a>
       filmed a short documentary about this city in 1912,
       <i>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=L%27antique_Tol%C3%A8de&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="L'antique Tolède (page does not exist)">
         L'antique Tolède
        </a>
       </i>
       (The Old Toledo). This is probably the first film about Toledo.
      </p>
